<script type="text/javascript">
//<![CDATA[



/* JQUERY */
jQuery(document).ready(function(){ 
    
   
  

	/* jQuery('ul#rmenu').superfish(); */
	/* jQuery('ul#rmenu').superfish().find('ul').bgIframe({opacity:false}); */
 
	/* For IE6 */
	if (jQuery.browser.msie && /MSIE 6\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent) && !/MSIE 7\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent) && !/MSIE 8\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent)) {

		/* Max-width for images in IE6 */		
		var centerwidth = jQuery("td#middle").width(); 
		
		/* Images without caption */
		jQuery(".post img").each(function() { 
			var maxwidth = centerwidth - 10 + 'px';
			var imgwidth = jQuery(this).width(); 
			var imgheight = jQuery(this).height(); 
			var newimgheight = (centerwidth / imgwidth * imgheight) + 'px';	
			if (imgwidth > centerwidth) { 
				jQuery(this).css({width: maxwidth}); 
				jQuery(this).css({height: newimgheight}); 
			}
		});
		
		/* Images with caption */
		jQuery("div.wp-caption").each(function() { 
			var captionwidth = jQuery(this).width(); 
			var maxcaptionwidth = centerwidth + 'px';
			var captionheight = jQuery(this).height();
			var captionimgwidth =  jQuery("div.wp-caption img").width();
			var captionimgheight =  jQuery("div.wp-caption img").height();
			if (captionwidth > centerwidth) { 
				jQuery(this).css({width: maxcaptionwidth}); 
				var newcaptionheight = (centerwidth / captionwidth * captionheight) + 'px';
				var newcaptionimgheight = (centerwidth / captionimgwidth * captionimgheight) + 'px';
				jQuery(this).css({height: newcaptionheight}); 
				jQuery("div.wp-caption img").css({height: newcaptionimgheight}); 
				}
		});
		
		/* sfhover for LI:HOVER support in IE6: */
		jQuery("ul li").
			hover( function() {
					jQuery(this).addClass("sfhover")
				}, 
				function() {
					jQuery(this).removeClass("sfhover")
				} 
			); 

	/* End IE6 */
	}
	
	
	
	/* Since 3.7.8: Auto resize videos (embed and iframe elements) 
	TODO: Parse parent's dimensions only once per layout column, not per video
	*/
	function bfa_resize_video() {
		jQuery('embed, iframe').each( function() {
			var video = jQuery(this),
			videoWidth = video.attr('width'); // use the attr here, not width() or css()
			videoParent = video.parent(),
			videoParentWidth = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'width' ) ),
			videoParentBorder = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'border-left-width' ) ) 
										+  parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'border-right-width' ) ),
			videoParentPadding = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'padding-left' ) ) 
										+  parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'padding-right' ) ),
			maxWidth = videoParentWidth - videoParentBorder - videoParentPadding;

			if( videoWidth > maxWidth ) {
				var videoHeight = video.attr('height'),
				videoMaxHeight = ( maxWidth / videoWidth * videoHeight );
				video.attr({ width: maxWidth, height: videoMaxHeight });
			} 

		});	
	}
	bfa_resize_video();
	jQuery(window).resize( bfa_resize_video );

		
	jQuery(".post table tr").
		mouseover(function() {
			jQuery(this).addClass("over");
		}).
		mouseout(function() {
			jQuery(this).removeClass("over");
		});

	
	jQuery(".post table tr:even").
		addClass("alt");

	
	jQuery("input.text, input.TextField, input.file, input.password, textarea").
		focus(function () {  
			jQuery(this).addClass("highlight"); 
		}).
		blur(function () { 
			jQuery(this).removeClass("highlight"); 
		})
	
	jQuery("input.inputblur").
		focus(function () {  
			jQuery(this).addClass("inputfocus"); 
		}).
		blur(function () { 
			jQuery(this).removeClass("inputfocus"); 
		})

		

	
	jQuery("input.button, input.Button, input#submit").
		mouseover(function() {
			jQuery(this).addClass("buttonhover");
		}).
		mouseout(function() {
			jQuery(this).removeClass("buttonhover");
		});

	/* toggle "you can use these xhtml tags" */
	jQuery("a.xhtmltags").
		click(function(){ 
			jQuery("div.xhtml-tags").slideToggle(300); 
		});

	/* For the Tabbed Widgets plugin: */
	jQuery("ul.tw-nav-list").
		addClass("clearfix");

		
	
});

//]]>
</script>

								<div class="post-102 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-cpp-tutorial odd" id="post-102">
						<div class="post-headline">		<h1>6.9 &#8212; Dynamic memory allocation with new and delete</h1>
		</div>		<div class="post-byline">By Alex, on July 13th, 2007</div>		<div class="post-bodycopy clearfix"><p>All of the variables used up to this point in the tutorial have one thing in common: the variables must be declared at compile time.  This leads to two issues: First, it&#8217;s difficult to conditionally declare a variable, outside of putting it in an if statement block (in which case it will go out of scope when the block ends).  Second, the size of all arrays must be decided upon in advance of the program being run.  For example, the following is not legal:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac11c6190834912" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11c6190834912-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11c6190834912-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11c6190834912-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11c6190834912-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11c6190834912-5">5</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11c6190834912-1"><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"How many variables do you want? "</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11c6190834912-2"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">nVars</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11c6190834912-3"><span class="crayon-v">cin</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&gt;&gt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">nVars</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11c6190834912-4">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11c6190834912-5"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">anArray</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-v">nVars</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// wrong!&nbsp;&nbsp;The size of the array must be a constant</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0014 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>However, there are many cases where it would be useful to be able to size or resize arrays while the program is being run.  For example, we may want to use a string to hold someone&#8217;s name, but we do not know how long their name is until they enter it.  Or we may want to read in a number of records from disk, but we don&#8217;t know in advance how many records there are.  Or we may be creating a game, with a variable number of monsters chasing the player.</p>
<p>If we have to declare the size of everything at compile time, the best we can do is try to make a guess the maximum number of variables we&#8217;ll need and hope that&#8217;s enough:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac11d7678053467" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11d7678053467-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11d7678053467-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11d7678053467-3">3</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11d7678053467-1"><span class="crayon-t">char</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">szName</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-cn">25</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// let's hope their name is less than 25 chars!</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11d7678053467-2"><span class="crayon-e">Record </span><span class="crayon-v">asRecordArray</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-cn">500</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// let's hope there are less than 500 records!</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11d7678053467-3"><span class="crayon-e">Monster </span><span class="crayon-v">asMonsterArray</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-cn">20</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// 20 monsters maximum</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0013 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>This is a poor solution for several reasons.  First, it leads to wasted memory if the variables aren&#8217;t actually used.  For example, if we allocate 25 chars for every name, but names on average are only 12 chars long, we&#8217;re allocating over twice what we really need!  Second, it can lead to artificial limitations and/or buffer overflows.  What happens when the user tries to read in 600 records from disk?  Because we&#8217;ve only allocated 500 spaces, either we have to give the user an error, only read the first 500 records, or (in the worst case where we don&#8217;t handle this case at all), we overflow the record buffer and our program crashes.</p>
<p>Fortunately, these problems are easily solved via dynamic memory allocation.  <strong>Dynamic memory allocation</strong> allows us to allocate memory of whatever size we want when we need it.</p>
<p><strong>Dynamically allocating single variables</strong></p>
<p>To allocate a <em>single</em> variable dynamically, we use the scalar (non-array) form of the <strong>new</strong> operator:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac11df675718963" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11df675718963-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11df675718963-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">new</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// dynamically allocate an integer</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0007 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>The new operator returns the <i>address</i> of the variable that has been allocated.  This address can be stored in a pointer, and the pointer can then be dereferenced to access the variable.</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac11e6696699023" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11e6696699023-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11e6696699023-2">2</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11e6696699023-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">new</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// dynamically allocate an integer</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11e6696699023-2"><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">7</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// assign 7 to this integer</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0011 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>When we are done with a dynamically allocated variable, we need to explicitly tell C++ to free the memory for reuse.  This is done via the scalar (non-array) form of the <strong>delete</strong> operator:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac11ec542461900" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11ec542461900-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11ec542461900-2">2</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11ec542461900-1"><span class="crayon-e">delete </span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// unallocate memory assigned to pnValue</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11ec542461900-2"><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0008 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Note that the delete operator does not delete the pointer -- it deletes the memory that the pointer points to!</p>
<p><strong>Dynamically allocating arrays</strong></p>
<p>Declaring arrays dynamically allows us to choose their size while the program is running.  To allocate an array dynamically, we use the array form of new and delete (often called new[] and delete[]):</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac11f3992096959" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11f3992096959-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11f3992096959-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11f3992096959-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11f3992096959-4">4</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11f3992096959-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">nSize</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">12</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11f3992096959-2"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pnArray</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">new</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-v">nSize</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// note: nSize does not need to be constant!</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11f3992096959-3"><span class="crayon-v">pnArray</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-cn">4</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">7</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11f3992096959-4"><span class="crayon-v">delete</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">pnArray</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0018 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Because we are allocating an array, C++ knows that it should use the array version of new instead of the scalar version of new.   Essentially, the new[] operator is called, even though the [] isn&#8217;t placed next to the new keyword.</p>
<p>When deleting a dynamically allocated array, we have to use the array version of delete, which is delete[].  This tells the CPU that it needs to clean up multiple variables instead of a single variable.</p>
<p>Note that array access is done the same way with dynamically allocated arrays as with normal arrays.  While this might look slightly funny, given that pnArray is explicitly declared as a pointer, remember that arrays are really just pointers in C++ anyway.</p>
<p>One of the most common mistakes that new programmers make when dealing with dynamic memory allocation is to use delete instead of delete[] when deleting a dynamically allocated array.  Do not do this!  Using the scalar version of delete on an array can cause data corruption or other problems.</p>
<p><strong>Memory leaks</strong></p>
<p>Dynamically allocated memory effectively has no scope.  That is, it stays allocated until it is explicitly deallocated or until the program ends.  However, the pointers used to access dynamically allocated memory follow the scoping rules of normal variables.  This mismatch can create interesting problems.</p>
<p>Consider the following function:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac11fb459129450" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11fb459129450-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11fb459129450-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11fb459129450-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac11fb459129450-4">4</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11fb459129450-1"><span class="crayon-t">void</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">doSomething</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11fb459129450-2"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11fb459129450-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">new</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac11fb459129450-4"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0010 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>This function allocates an integer dynamically, but never frees it using delete.  Because pointers follow all of the same rules as normal variables, when the function ends, pnValue will go out of scope.  Because pnValue is the only variable holding the address of the dynamically allocated integer, when pnValue is destroyed there are no more references to the dynamically allocated memory.  This is called a <strong>memory leak</strong>.  As a result, the dynamically allocated integer can not be deleted, and thus can not be reallocated or reused.  Memory leaks eat up free memory while the program is running, making less memory available not only to this program, but to other programs as well.  Programs with severe memory leak problems can eat all the available memory, causing the entire machine to run slowly or even crash.</p>
<p>Memory leaks can also result if the pointer holding the address of the dynamically allocated memory is reassigned to another value:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac1203594642557" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac1203594642557-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac1203594642557-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac1203594642557-3">3</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac1203594642557-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">nValue</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">5</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac1203594642557-2"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">new</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac1203594642557-3"><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">&amp;nValue</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// old address lost, memory leak results</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0013 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>It is also possible to get a memory leak via double-allocation:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac1209870471534" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac1209870471534-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac1209870471534-2">2</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac1209870471534-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">new</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac1209870471534-2"><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">new</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// old address lost, memory leak results</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0010 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>The address returned from the second allocation overwrites the address of the first allocation.  Consequently, the first allocation becomes a memory leak!</p>
<p><strong>Null pointers (part II)</strong></p>
<p>Null pointers (pointers set to address 0) are particularly useful when dealing with dynamic memory allocation.  A null pointer basically says &#8220;no memory has been allocated yet&#8221;.  This allows us to do things like conditionally allocate memory:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac1210592570579" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac1210592570579-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac1210592570579-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac1210592570579-3">3</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac1210592570579-1"><span class="crayon-c">// If pnValue isn't already allocated, allocate it</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac1210592570579-2"><span class="crayon-st">if</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-o">!</span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac1210592570579-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">new</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0008 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Keep in mind that just like normal variables, when a pointer is created, it&#8217;s value is undefined.  Consequently, it is a good idea to set all pointers that are not used right away to 0:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac1216476950905" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac1216476950905-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac1216476950905-2">2</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac1216476950905-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">new</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac1216476950905-2"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pnOtherValue</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// will allocate later</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0007 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Similarly, when a dynamically allocated variable is deleted, the pointer pointing to it is not zero&#8217;d.  Consider the following snippet:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac121c287130793" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac121c287130793-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac121c287130793-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac121c287130793-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac121c287130793-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac121c287130793-5">5</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac121c287130793-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">new</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac121c287130793-2"><span class="crayon-e">delete </span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// pnValue not set to 0</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac121c287130793-3">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac121c287130793-4"><span class="crayon-st">if</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac121c287130793-5"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">5</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// will cause a crash</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0010 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Because pnValue has not been set to 0, the if statement condition evaluates to true, and the program tries to assign 5 to deallocated memory.  This almost inevitably will cause a program to crash.  It is never a good idea to leave a pointer pointing to deallocated memory.  When deallocating memory, set the pointer that has been deallocated to 0 immediately afterward.  This helps ensure the program does not try and access memory that has already been deallocated.  The above program should be written as:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac1223256138243" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac1223256138243-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac1223256138243-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac1223256138243-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac1223256138243-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac1223256138243-5">5</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac1223256138243-6">6</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac1223256138243-7">7</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac1223256138243-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">new</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac1223256138243-2"><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">7</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac1223256138243-3"><span class="crayon-e">delete </span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac1223256138243-4"><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac1223256138243-5">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac1223256138243-6"><span class="crayon-st">if</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac1223256138243-7"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">5</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0012 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Get in the habit of assigning your pointers to 0 both when they are declared (unless assigned to another address), and after they are deleted.  It will save you a lot of grief.</p>
<p>Finally, deleting a null pointer has no effect.  Thus, there is no need for the following:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac122a160951227" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac122a160951227-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac122a160951227-2">2</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac122a160951227-1"><span class="crayon-st">if</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac122a160951227-2"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-e">delete </span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0004 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Instead, you can just write:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac1230824349744" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac1230824349744-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac1230824349744-1"><span class="crayon-e">delete </span><span class="crayon-v">pnValue</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0002 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>If pnValue is non-null, the dynamically allocated variable will be deleted.  If it is null, nothing will happen.</p>

		<p>New C++ programmers should be notified that there is a fundamental design flaw in C++ (and perhaps any language, allowing explicitly freeing memory) - there is no way to set to null all pointers referencing same memory address, other than knowing/remembering them. Which is affected by &#8220;human factors&#8221;, and thus can not be reliable. Thats where reference counting and garbage collectors comes in&#8230;</p>
		</div>

		<p>The new operator is used to create the object dynamically. Using the new operator the memory is allocated and the constructor of the class gets called for that memory.<br />
 Using the delete the destructor of the class gets called and the memory is released which is allocated by new.<br />
very useful content for more information refer  <a href="http://www.cpptutorials.com/2014/11/memory-allocation-de-allocation-using.html" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-comment', 'http://www.cpptutorials.com/2014/11/memory-allocation-de-allocation-using.html', 'Memory allocation, de-allocation using new and delete with examples and syntax ']);" rel="nofollow">Memory allocation, de-allocation using new and delete with examples and syntax </a></p>

		<p>That is a great point, Sergk.  Thanks for bringing it up.</p>
<p>What Sergk is talking about is the fact that you can have multiple pointers pointing to the same bit of dynamically allocated memory.  Let&#8217;s say you do something like this:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac6d65737652273" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac6d65737652273-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pnPtr1</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">new</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac6d65737652273-2"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pnPtr2</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">pnPtr1</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>

<p></p>
<p>Now both pointers point to the dynamically allocated memory.  However, if you do this:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac6d70868023384" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">

					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac6d70868023384-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac6d70868023384-2">2</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac6d70868023384-1"><span class="crayon-e">delete </span><span class="crayon-v">pnPtr1</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac6d70868023384-2"><span class="crayon-v">pnPtr1</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>

<p></p>
<p>pnPtr2 is left pointing to deallocated memory!  And thus a call like this:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac6d76185031742" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac6d76185031742-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac6d76185031742-2">2</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac6d76185031742-1"><span class="crayon-st">if</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-v">pnPtr2</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac6d76185031742-2"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pnPtr2</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">5</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0004 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>will cause your program to crash, even though it seems like it should be okay.</p>
<p>There are various technique for getting around this behavior (as mentioned, reference counting and garbage collection), some of which C++ support and some of which it doesn&#8217;t.  From a coding standpoint, perhaps the best solution is simply to avoid having multiple pointers to the same bit of memory, though this isn&#8217;t always reasonable.</p>
		</div>

		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-5930">
		<div id="div-comment-5930" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/69-dynamic-memory-allocation-with-new-and-delete/#comment-5930">
		January 12, 2008 at 11:19 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/69-dynamic-memory-allocation-with-new-and-delete/?replytocom=5930#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-5930", "5930", "respond", "102" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>1) Each &#8220;chunk&#8221; of memory has to have a unique address, otherwise there&#8217;d be no way to address that chunk of memory individually.  On the 80&#215;86 architecture, the size of that &#8220;chunk&#8221; is a byte, which means we can address individual bytes.  The address of 0 is used to mean &#8220;not pointing to anything&#8221;.</p>
<p>2) My understanding is that the program/memory system keeps track of how large your arrays are (I am not sure how this happens behind the scenes).  In any case, when you delete the array, it already knows how much to delete.  Forcing the programmer to specify that amount would be redundant and lead to overspecification errors (eg. what if the programmer allocated 10 bytes but then tried to delete 8?)</p>
<p>3) Thanks, I&#8217;ll get that fixed.</p>
		</div>

		<p>I&#8217;m working on an assignment for a course I&#8217;m taking and we are to create two classes; Vertex and Polygon, with the Polygon class consisting of an array of Vertices. The array of Vertices is dynamically allocated, and I have two constructors:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac6adc094256079" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">

<p>But if a create a Polygon with the default constructor and then add three Vertices the program crashes. The weird thing though is that the crash doesn&#8217;t seem to come until I have come to the last line (delete[] tmp;), but only when I add the third Vertex. The firs two go fine. Any ideas as to why this happens?</p>

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-9068">
		<div id="div-comment-9068" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/69-dynamic-memory-allocation-with-new-and-delete/#comment-9068">
		March 7, 2008 at 7:23 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/69-dynamic-memory-allocation-with-new-and-delete/?replytocom=9068#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-9068", "9068", "respond", "102" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>I see a couple of things done incorrectly here.  First, in your constructor, you assign vertices = vert;  You seem to be assuming this will copy the incoming elements, but it won&#8217;t.  It&#8217;ll simply set vertices to point to those elements.</p>
<p>This is asking for trouble.  If the user passes in a non-dynamically allocated vertex array, you will end up with the vertex pointer pointing to a local variable that will eventually go out of scope.  When it does, and you try to access it, you program will crash.</p>
<p>Instead, it is safer to allocate a new dynamic vertex array inside your constructor and then copy the vertices to it individually (using a for loop).  This way you can guarantee that your vertices will persist even if the user passes in vertices that have been non-dynamically allocated.</p>
<p>Second, to see why Add() crashes, simply step through your code when vertices is non-null (which it is when you&#8217;ve called the above constructor):</p>
<p>In this case, the if condition is true, so the conditional executes.  tmp is set to vertices.  Because tmp and vertices are both pointers, this simply does a pointer assignment.  It does not copy the vertices!  So when you delete vertices, you also delete what tmp is pointing to.  Consequently, after the conditional, tmp is pointing to garbage.  tmp[numVerts] = newVert tries to write a vertex into unallocated memory.  Then later, you delete tmp, which is already pointing to unallocated memory.  Trying to delete unallocated memory will always crash your program.</p>
<p>You basically have the right idea, you&#8217;ve just assumed that assigning one pointer to another will copy the elements, and it won&#8217;t.  It&#8217;ll just make them point to the same thing.</p>
<p>Your add function should look like this:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-5">5</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-6">6</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-7">7</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-8">8</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-9">9</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-10">10</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-11">11</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-12">12</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-13">13</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-14">14</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-15">15</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-1"><span class="crayon-t">void</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">add</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-e">Vertex </span><span class="crayon-v">newVert</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-2"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span class="crayon-v">Vertex</span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">tmp</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">new</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">Vertex</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-v">numVerts</span><span class="crayon-o">+</span><span class="crayon-cn">1</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-4"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span class="crayon-st">if</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-v">vertices</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-5"><span class="crayon-c">// copy your old vertices into temp.&nbsp;&nbsp;This will involve using a for loop</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-6"><span class="crayon-c">// and copying them individually</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-7"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-v">delete</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">vertices</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-8"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-9"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span class="crayon-v">tmp</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-v">numVerts</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">newVert</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-10"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span class="crayon-v">vertices</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">new</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">Vertex</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-o">++</span><span class="crayon-v">numVerts</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// you don't need this</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-11"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span class="crayon-v">vertices</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">tmp</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-12"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span class="crayon-v">delete</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">tmp</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// or this</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-13">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-14"><span class="crayon-c">// increment numVerts here</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac69d6177785861-15"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0023 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>This way, you allocate a new temp array, copy elements from the old array to the new array, delete the old array, and then set the old array to point to the new one.</p>
		</div>

		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-30004">
		<div id="div-comment-30004" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/69-dynamic-memory-allocation-with-new-and-delete/#comment-30004">
		October 14, 2008 at 6:37 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/69-dynamic-memory-allocation-with-new-and-delete/?replytocom=30004#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-30004", "30004", "respond", "102" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>It&#8217;s the delete keyword that does the deallocation, not the setting to 0.  If you set a pointer to 0, the memory originally allocated will be lost forever (well, until the program is cleaned up by the operating system), unless you have another pointer pointing to it.  I make a habit of setting my deleted pointers to 0 because having a pointer to deallocated memory can and usually does lead to problems as well.</p>
<p>If you do int *pnValue2 = pnValue, then pnValue2 and pnValue both point to the same address, and they should give you the same dereference because the dereference of a pointer is just the value at the address the pointer is pointing to.  Now, if you delete pnValue or pnValue2, the address that BOTH point to is deallocated.  From that point forward, if you use either one while they point to deallocated memory, you&#8217;ll be in trouble.  One common mistake C++ newbies make is to delete pnValue and set it to 0, and forget that pnValue2 points to the same deallocated location.  Then, when they try to access pnValue2, their program crashes.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->

				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac6618064904026-1"><span class="crayon-m">const</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">myarray</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">{</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">1</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">2</span><span class="crayon-sy">,</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">3</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>

		<div id="div-comment-31566" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/69-dynamic-memory-allocation-with-new-and-delete/#comment-31566">
		November 3, 2008 at 7:01 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/69-dynamic-memory-allocation-with-new-and-delete/?replytocom=31566#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-31566", "31566", "respond", "102" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>There are a couple of options.  If you want an array that is shared by all members of your class, you could make the array in your class static and define it in the cpp file just like you do above (see the lesson on <a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/811-static-member-variables/" rel="nofollow">static member variables for more info</a>).</p>
<p>If you want a per-class array, my advice would be to stop using C-style arrays altogether and use std::vector, then push values onto the vector in your class constructor.</p>
		</div>

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-4 clearfix" id="comment-31637">
		<div id="div-comment-31637" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/69-dynamic-memory-allocation-with-new-and-delete/#comment-31637">
		November 4, 2008 at 10:45 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/69-dynamic-memory-allocation-with-new-and-delete/?replytocom=31637#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-31637", "31637", "respond", "102" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Static members are kind of funny -- they&#8217;re members of the class, but you don&#8217;t need an instantiated class member to access them.  You can access it directly via using the class name and the scope operator (eg. MyClass::s_nMyStaticInt).  It&#8217;s more or less identical to having a global variable inside a namespace, except the class is the &#8220;container&#8221; for the variable instead of the namespace.  Static members are essentially globally scoped.</p>
		</div>

		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/69-dynamic-memory-allocation-with-new-and-delete/#comment-32306">
		November 17, 2008 at 7:32 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/69-dynamic-memory-allocation-with-new-and-delete/?replytocom=32306#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-32306", "32306", "respond", "102" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Most modern operating systems will clean up for you when the program exits.</p>
<p>That said, it&#8217;s not a good idea to rely on the OS to do this for you.  This is less true when doing little sample programs, but once you start writing larger programs having lots of memory leaks can really bog down your entire system, especially if you&#8217;re not running on much memory.</p>
		</div>

		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/69-dynamic-memory-allocation-with-new-and-delete/?replytocom=32954#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-32954", "32954", "respond", "102" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>When it comes to dynamically allocated arrays in C++, you have to save the size independently of the array.  There&#8217;s no way to derive it from the array, unfortunately.</p>
<p>The sizeof(anArray) / sizeof(anArray[0]) trick only works if anArray is a static array (eg. declared as int anArray[5]).</p>
<p>Your algorithm doesn&#8217;t really work because you loop on the size of the array, which presumes you already know it.  If you already know it, there&#8217;s no reason to go through the whole process of trying to find it. <img src="http://www.learncpp.com/blog/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" /></p>
		</div>

<p>Code effectively allows the user to define the arrays size while the program is running.</p>

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/69-dynamic-memory-allocation-with-new-and-delete/?replytocom=39089#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-39089", "39089", "respond", "102" )' aria-label='Reply to Pathik'> &middot; Reply</a></span>

		<p>How do you dynamically allocate a multidimensional array?</p>
<p>This does&#8217;nt work:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-48407">
		<div id="div-comment-48407" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/69-dynamic-memory-allocation-with-new-and-delete/#comment-48407">
		March 1, 2009 at 11:16 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/69-dynamic-memory-allocation-with-new-and-delete/?replytocom=48407#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-48407", "48407", "respond", "102" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>This is correct.  Remember that a pointer stores an address, and when you dereference a pointer, it gets the value at that address.  Thus, if you store the address of 0 in a pointer, when you dereference it, it tries to get the value at address 0.  This is generally protected memory and will cause your OS to crash or throw an exception.</p>
<p>If you want to get or set a value via pointer, the pointer has to point to allocated, valid memory.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->

<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1 clearfix" id="comment-48443">
		<div id="div-comment-48443" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/69-dynamic-memory-allocation-with-new-and-delete/#comment-48443">
		March 1, 2009 at 12:11 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/69-dynamic-memory-allocation-with-new-and-delete/?replytocom=48443#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-48443", "48443", "respond", "102" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>There are three primary reasons to use pointers:</p>
<p>1) When you allocate memory using new, that memory does not go out of scope when the function ends (although the pointer pointing to it will).  This can be desirable in some cases.</p>
<p>2) When working with arrays, you have to use a pointer in order to do dynamically sized arrays.  You can not do something like this:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d744ac5c08349853545" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac5c08349853545-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac5c08349853545-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">anArray</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-v">nSize</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0003 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>3) When working with large chunks of memory, it is better to allocate them on the heap (dynamically, using new) than the stack (via a normal variable).</p>
		</div>

		</div>
		<p>I believe this is because delete[] only releases the memory referenced by ptr, it does not destroy the information already stored in them. That is why you can still view them, as ptr still stores the same memory address, and the data you defined before still resides in those very same addresses.</p>
<p>However, you should ask somebody who knows this better!</p>

					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d744ac58c6342306527-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d744ac58c6342306527-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">matrix1</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">new</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-v">row</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-v">col</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0006 seconds] -->
<p>(row and col being variables)</p>

<p>It compiles without warnings, but it does not actually assign the value to the cell with adress (0x00345D45). Instead, when printing to the console the value referenced by p instead of &#8216;8&#8217; I get something like -55634323. It seems pointers can operate on memory only when the memory location has been named (through a variable declaration), or when it is dynamically allocated.</p>

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/69-dynamic-memory-allocation-with-new-and-delete/?replytocom=95032#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-95032", "95032", "respond", "102" )' aria-label='Reply to fmunshi'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Hi Alex,</p>
<p>In your explanation of Null Pointers (Part II) it seems you have a typo in the third code snippet:</p>
<p>1	int *pnValue = new int;<br />
2	delete pnValue; // pnValue not set to 0<br />
3<br />
4	if (pnValue)<br />
5	    *pnValue = 5; // will cause a crash</p>
<p>You should add the following between line 1 and line 2:<br />
*pnValue = 7;</p>
<p>Since in the fourth code snippet where you correct the Null pointer error you have &#8220;*pnValue = 7;&#8221; already inserted, it might confuse some people into thinking that assigning *pnValue to 7 has something to do with fixing the Null pointer.</p>
<p>Thanks for the excellent tutorials!!!<br />
Fardan</p>
		</div>

		March 1, 2015 at 12:55 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/69-dynamic-memory-allocation-with-new-and-delete/?replytocom=251676#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251676", "251676", "respond", "102" )' aria-label='Reply to Sergi'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Hi Alex,</p>
<p>congratulations, it is possibly the best explanation of what pointers are and how to deal with them that I&apos;ve ever seen.</p>
<p>I just wanted to point out two things that, if I unterstood everything correctly, maybe you should include in your tutorial:</p>
<p>1)The code you use to explain how to dinamically allocate arrays should include another statement, because the pointer pnArray still holds the adress of the deleted memory at the end of your code.</p>
<p>int nSize = 12;<br />
int *pnArray = new int[nSize]; // note: nSize does not need to be constant!<br />
pnArray[4] = 7;<br />
delete[] pnArray;<br />
pnArray = 0;            // added line to your code</p>
<p>2) It would be useful to explain that trying to evaluate a pointer that was zero&apos;d causes a program crash. Take for example the following:</p>
<p>int* pnArray = 0;<br />
cout &lt;&lt; &quot;pnArray points to the adress: &quot; &lt;&lt; pnArray &lt;&lt; endl;&nbsp;&nbsp;// program crash!</p>
<p>Please tell me if I&apos;m wrong or if I have unterstood it just right, thanks!</p>
		</div>
